## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) depends on velocity v and time t. The equation of motion likely involves damping terms (velocity-dependent), possible restoring forces implicitly encoded, and potentially time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple linear velocity-dependent force)
- Damped oscillator velocity form: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (damping plus sinusoidal driving)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity (van der Pol type): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (amplitude-dependent damping with drive)
- Quadratic-cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping with harmonic restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) (parametrically modulated system)
- Duffing-like via velocity: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Harmonic restoring with velocity damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v (position encoded as integral of velocity)
- Nonlinear damping with harmonic drive: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 - v**2) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (limit cycle oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)
- Mixed time-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (modulated nonlinear system)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (parametric instability form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Limit cycle behavior (self-sustained oscillation) ŌåÆ terms like (1 - c*v┬▓)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change
- Odd-symmetry in velocity (symmetric oscillation) ŌåÆ only odd powers of v appear (v, v┬│, vŌüĄ) indicating no preferred direction
- Harmonic driving force ŌåÆ sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) representing external periodic forcing
- Parametric excitation ŌåÆ products of v with periodic functions of t, i.e., v*cos(c*t), indicating time-varying system parameters
- Energy-dependent damping ŌåÆ polynomial in v┬▓ multiplied by v, such as v*(cŌéĆ + cŌéü*v┬▓), where damping coefficient depends on energy
- Phase-space reconstruction ŌåÆ when position x is absent, trigonometric functions of t can implicitly represent position for harmonic-like systems
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous distinction ŌåÆ if t appears only inside periodic functions, system is periodically driven; if t is absent, system is autonomous
- Soft/hard spring behavior ŌåÆ sign of cubic coefficient determines whether nonlinearity softens or hardens the effective restoring force
